It's not safe to do so if\n394: \t * the query contains anything parallel-unsafe; parallelModeOK will be\n395: \t * false in that case.  Note that parallelModeOK can't change after this\n396: \t * point. Otherwise, everything in the query is either parallel-safe or\n397: \t * parallel-restricted, and in either case it should be OK to impose\n398: \t * parallel-mode restrictions.  If that ends up breaking something, then\n399: \t * either some function the user included in the query is incorrectly\n400: \t * labeled as parallel-safe or parallel-restricted when in reality it's\n401: \t * parallel-unsafe, or else the query planner itself has a bug.\n402: \t */\n403: \tglob->parallelModeNeeded = glob->parallelModeOK &&\n404: \t\t(debug_parallel_query != DEBUG_PARALLEL_OFF);\n405: \n406: \t/* Determine what fraction of the plan is likely to be scanned */\n407: \tif (cursorOptions & CURSOR_OPT_FAST_PLAN)\n408: \t{\n409: \t\t/*\n410: \t\t * We have no real idea how many tuples the user will ultimately FETCH\n411: \t\t * from a cursor, but it is often the case that he doesn't want 'em\n412: \t\t * all, or would prefer a fast-start plan anyway so that he can\n413: \t\t * process some of the tuples sooner. The plan tree is essentially\\n7: a demand-pull pipeline of tuple processing operations.  Each node, when\\n8: called, will produce the next tuple in its output sequence, or NULL if no\\n9: more tuples are available.  If the node is not a primitive relation-scanning\\n10: node, it will have child node(s) that it calls in turn to obtain input\\n11: tuples.\\n12: \\n13: Refinements on this basic model include:\\n14: \\n15: * Choice of scan direction (forwards or backwards).  Caution: this is not\\n16: currently well-supported.  It works for primitive scan nodes, but not very\\n17: well for joins, aggregates, etc.\\n18: \\n19: * Rescan command to reset a node and make it generate its output sequence\\n20: over again.\\n21: \\n22: * Parameters that can alter a node's results.  After adjusting a parameter,\\n23: the rescan command must be applied to that node and all nodes above it.\\n24: There is a moderately intelligent scheme to avoid rescanning nodes\\n25: unnecessarily (for example, Sort does not rescan its input if no parameters\\n26: of the input have changed, since it can just reread its stored sorted data).\\n27: \\n28: For a SELECT, it is only necessary to deliver the top-level result tuples\\n29: to the client.  For INSERT/UPDATE/DELETE/MERGE, the actual table modification\\n30: operations happen in a top-level ModifyTable plan node.  If the query\\n31: includes a RETURNING clause, the ModifyTable node delivers the computed\\n32: RETURNING rows as output, otherwise it returns nothing.  Handling INSERT\\n33: is pretty straightforward: the tuples returned from the plan tree below\\n34: ModifyTable are inserted into the correct result relation.  For UPDATE,\\n35: the plan tree returns the new values of the updated columns, plus \\\"junk\\\"\\n36: (hidden) column(s) identifying which table row is to be updated.  The\\n37: ModifyTable node must fetch that row to extract values for the unchanged\\n38: columns, combine the values into a new row, and apply the update.  (For a\\n39: heap table, the row-identity junk column is a CTID, but other things may\\n40: be used for other table types.)  For DELETE, the plan tree need only deliver\\n41: junk row-identity column(s), and the ModifyTable node visits each of those\\n42: rows and marks the row deleted.  MERGE is described below.\\n43: \\n44: XXX a great deal more documentation needs to be written here...\\n45: \\n46: \\n47: Plan Trees and State Trees\\n48: --------------------------\\n49: \\n50: The plan tree delivered by the planner contains a tree of Plan nodes (struct\\n51: types derived from struct Plan).  During executor startup we build a parallel\\n52: tree of identical structure containing executor state nodes --- generally,\\n53: every plan node type has a corresponding executor state node type.  Each node\\n54: in the state tree has a pointer to its corresponding node in the plan tree,\\n55: plus executor state data as needed to implement that node type.  This\\n56: arrangement allows the plan tree to be completely read-only so far as the\\n57: executor is concerned: all data that is modified during execution is in the\\n58: state tree.  Read-only plan trees make life much simpler for plan caching and\\n59: reuse.\\n60: \\n61: A corresponding executor state node may not be created during executor startup\\n62: if the executor determines that an entire subplan is not required due to\\n63: execution time partition pruning determining that no matching records will be\\n64: found there.  This currently only occurs for Append and MergeAppend nodes.  In\\n65: this case the non-required subplans are ignored and the executor state's\\n66: subnode array will become out of sequence to the plan's subplan list.\\n67: \\n68: Each Plan node may have expression trees associated with it, to represent\\n69: its target list, qualification conditions, etc.  These trees are also\\n70: read-only to the executor, but the executor state for expression evaluation\\n71: does not mirror the Plan expression's tree shape, as explained below.\\n72: Rather, there's just one ExprState node per expression tree, although this\\n73: may have sub-nodes for some complex expression node types.\\n74: \\n75: Altogether there are four classes of nodes used in these trees: Plan nodes,\\n76: their corresponding PlanState nodes, Expr nodes, and ExprState nodes.\\n77: (Actually, there are also List nodes, which are used as \\\"glue\\\" in all\\n78: three tree-based representations.)\\n79: \\n80: \\n81: Expression Trees and ExprState nodes\\n82: ------------------------------------\\n83: \\n84: Expression trees, in contrast to Plan trees, are not mirrored into a\\n85: corresponding tree of state nodes.  Instead each separately executable\\n86: expression tree (e.g. a Plan's qual or targetlist) is represented by one\\n87: ExprState node.  The ExprState node contains the information needed to\\n88: evaluate the expression in a compact, linear form.  That compact form is\\n89: stored as a flat array in ExprState->steps[] (an array of ExprEvalStep,\\n90: not ExprEvalStep *).\\n91: \\n92: The reasons for choosing such a representation include:\\n93: - commonly the amount of work needed to evaluate one Expr-type node is\\n94:   small enough that the overhead of having to perform a tree-walk\\n95:   during evaluation is significant.\\n96: - the flat representation can be evaluated non-recursively within a single\\n97:   function, reducing stack depth and function call overhead.\\n98: - such a representation is usable both for fast interpreted execution,\\n99:   and for compiling into native code.\\n100: \\n101: The Plan-tree representation of an expression is compiled into an\\n102: ExprState node by ExecInitExpr().  As much complexity as possible should\\n103: be handled by ExecInitExpr() (and helpers), instead of execution time\\n104: where both interpreted and compiled versions would need to deal with the\\n105: complexity.  Besides duplicating effort between execution approaches,\\n106: runtime initialization checks also have a small but noticeable cost every\\n107: time the expression is evaluated.  Therefore, we allow ExecInitExpr() to\\n108: precompute information that we do not expect to vary across execution of a\\n109: single query, for example the set of CHECK constraint expressions to be\\n110: applied to a domain type.  This could not be done at plan time without\\n111: greatly increasing the number of events that require plan invalidation.\\n112: (Previously, some information of this kind was rechecked on each\\n113: expression evaluation, but that seems like unnecessary overhead.)\\n114: \\n115: \\n116: Expression Initialization\\n117: -------------------------\\n118: \\n119: During ExecInitExpr() and similar routines, Expr trees are converted\\n120: into the flat representation.  Each Expr node might be represented by\\n121: zero, one, or more ExprEvalSteps.\\n122: \\n123: Each ExprEvalStep's work is determined by its opcode (of enum ExprEvalOp)\\n124: and it stores the result of its work into the Datum variable and boolean\\n125: null flag variable pointed to by ExprEvalStep->resvalue/resnull.\\n126: Complex expressions are performed by chaining together several steps.\\n127: For example, \\\"a + b\\\" (one OpExpr, with two Var expressions) would be\\n128: represented as two steps to fetch the Var values, and one step for the\\n129: evaluation of the function underlying the + operator.  The steps for the\\n130: Vars would have their resvalue/resnull pointing directly to the appropriate\\n131: args[].value .isnull elements in the FunctionCallInfoBaseData struct that\\n132: is used by the function evaluation step, thus avoiding extra work to copy\\n133: the result values around.\\n134: \\n135: The last entry in a completed ExprState->steps array is always an\\n136: EEOP_DONE_RETURN or EEOP_DONE_NO_RETURN step; this removes the need to\\n137: test for end-of-array while iterating. The former is used when the\\n138: expression returns a value directly, the latter when side-effects of\\n139: expression initialization are the goal (e.g. for projection or\\n140: aggregate transition value computation).\\n141: \\n142: Also, if the expression contains any variable references (to user\\n143: columns of the ExprContext's INNER, OUTER, or SCAN tuples), the steps\\n144: array begins with EEOP_*_FETCHSOME steps that ensure that the relevant\\n145: tuples have been deconstructed to make the required columns directly\\n146: available (cf. slot_getsomeattrs()).  This allows individual Var-fetching\\n147: steps to be little more than an array lookup.\\n148: \\n149: Most of ExecInitExpr()'s work is done by the recursive function\\n150: ExecInitExprRec() and its subroutines. Handling INSERT\n33: is pretty straightforward: the tuples returned from the plan tree below\n34: ModifyTable are inserted into the correct result relation.  For UPDATE,\n35: the plan tree returns the new values of the updated columns, plus \"junk\"\n36: (hidden) column(s) identifying which table row is to be updated.  The\n37: ModifyTable node must fetch that row to extract values for the unchanged\n38: columns, combine the values into a new row, and apply the update.  (For a\n39: heap table, the row-identity junk column is a CTID, but other things may\n40: be used for other table types.)  For DELETE, the plan tree need only deliver\n41: junk row-identity column(s), and the ModifyTable node visits each of those\n42: rows and marks the row deleted.  MERGE is described below.\n43: \n44: XXX a great deal more documentation needs to be written here...\n45: \n46: \n47: Plan Trees and State Trees\n48: --------------------------\n49: \n50: The plan tree delivered by the planner contains a tree of Plan nodes (struct\n51: types derived from struct Plan).  During executor startup we build a parallel\n52: tree of identical structure containing executor state nodes --- generally,\n53: every plan node type has a corresponding executor state node type.  Each node\n54: in the state tree has a pointer to its corresponding node in the plan tree,\n55: plus executor state data as needed to implement that node type.  This\n56: arrangement allows the plan tree to be completely read-only so far as the\n57: executor is concerned: all data that is modified during execution is in the\n58: state tree.  Read-only plan trees make life much simpler for plan caching and\n59: reuse.\n60: \n61: A corresponding executor state node may not be created during executor startup\n62: if the executor determines that an entire subplan is not required due to\n63: execution time partition pruning determining that no matching records will be\n64: found there.  This currently only occurs for Append and MergeAppend nodes.  In\n65: this case the non-required subplans are ignored and the executor state's\n66: subnode array will become out of sequence to the plan's subplan list.\n67: \n68: Each Plan node may have expression trees associated with it, to represent\n69: its target list, qualification conditions, etc.  These trees are also\n70: read-only to the executor, but the executor state for expression evaluation\n71: does not mirror the Plan expression's tree shape, as explained below.\n72: Rather, there's just one ExprState node per expression tree, although this\n73: may have sub-nodes for some complex expression node types.\n74: \n75: Altogether there are four classes of nodes used in these trees: Plan nodes,\n76: their corresponding PlanState nodes, Expr nodes, and ExprState nodes.\n77: (Actually, there are also List nodes, which are used as \"glue\" in all\n78: three tree-based representations.)\n79: \n80: \n81: Expression Trees and ExprState nodes\n82: ------------------------------------\n83: \n84: Expression trees, in contrast to Plan trees, are not mirrored into a\n85: corresponding tree of state nodes.  Instead each separately executable\n86: expression tree (e.g. a Plan's qual or targetlist) is represented by one\n87: ExprState node.  The ExprState node contains the information needed to\n88: evaluate the expression in a compact, linear form.  That compact form is\n89: stored as a flat array in ExprState->steps[] (an array of ExprEvalStep,\n90: not ExprEvalStep *).\n91: \n92: The reasons for choosing such a representation include:\n93: - commonly the amount of work needed to evaluate one Expr-type node is\n94:   small enough that the overhead of having to perform a tree-walk\n95:   during evaluation is significant.\n96: - the flat representation can be evaluated non-recursively within a single\n97:   function, reducing stack depth and function call overhead.\n98: - such a representation is usable both for fast interpreted execution,\n99:   and for compiling into native code.\n100: \n101: The Plan-tree representation of an expression is compiled into an\n102: ExprState node by ExecInitExpr().  As much complexity as possible should\n103: be handled by ExecInitExpr() (and helpers), instead of execution time\n104: where both interpreted and compiled versions would need to deal with the\n105: complexity.  Besides duplicating effort between execution approaches,\n106: runtime initialization checks also have a small but noticeable cost every\n107: time the expression is evaluated.  Therefore, we allow ExecInitExpr() to\n108: precompute information that we do not expect to vary across execution of a\n109: single query, for example the set of CHECK constraint expressions to be\n110: applied to a domain type.  This could not be done at plan time without\n111: greatly increasing the number of events that require plan invalidation.\n112: (Previously, some information of this kind was rechecked on each\n113: expression evaluation, but that seems like unnecessary overhead.)\n114: \n115: \n116: Expression Initialization\n117: -------------------------\n118: \n119: During ExecInitExpr() and similar routines, Expr trees are converted\n120: into the flat representation.  Each Expr node might be represented by\n121: zero, one, or more ExprEvalSteps.\n122: \n123: Each ExprEvalStep's work is determined by its opcode (of enum ExprEvalOp)\n124: and it stores the result of its work into the Datum variable and boolean\n125: null flag variable pointed to by ExprEvalStep->resvalue/resnull.\n126: Complex expressions are performed by chaining together several steps.\n127: For example, \"a + b\" (one OpExpr, with two Var expressions) would be\n128: represented as two steps to fetch the Var values, and one step for the\n129: evaluation of the function underlying the + operator.  The steps for the\n130: Vars would have their resvalue/resnull pointing directly to the appropriate\n131: args[].value .isnull elements in the FunctionCallInfoBaseData struct that\n132: is used by the function evaluation step, thus avoiding extra work to copy\n133: the result values around.\n134: \n135: The last entry in a completed ExprState->steps array is always an\n136: EEOP_DONE_RETURN or EEOP_DONE_NO_RETURN step; this removes the need to\n137: test for end-of-array while iterating. The former is used when the\n138: expression returns a value directly, the latter when side-effects of\n139: expression initialization are the goal (e.g. for projection or\n140: aggregate transition value computation).\n141: \n142: Also, if the expression contains any variable references (to user\n143: columns of the ExprContext's INNER, OUTER, or SCAN tuples), the steps\n144: array begins with EEOP_*_FETCHSOME steps that ensure that the relevant\n145: tuples have been deconstructed to make the required columns directly\n146: available (cf. slot_getsomeattrs()).  This allows individual Var-fetching\n147: steps to be little more than an array lookup.\n148: \n149: Most of ExecInitExpr()'s work is done by the recursive function\n150: ExecInitExprRec() and its subroutines.  ExecInitExprRec() maps one Expr\n151: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-benchmarks/postgres--5a461dc4@eb8f07549ee15f0db57589c5f333de3f874fe855/-/blob/src/backend/executor/README%3FL1-150"}}}

calls `ExecutePlan()` to pull tuples\n  - `ExecutorEnd()` — Cleanup via `ExecEndNode()`\n- **src/backend/executor/execProcnode.c** — **Volcano-style Dispatch**: Core dispatcher implementing the pull-based iterator model:\n  - `ExecInitNode()` — Recursively initializes plan nodes; dispatches via switch on node tag to node-specific `ExecInit*()` functions\n  - `ExecProcNode()` — Main tuple-pulling dispatch (defined in executor.h as inline); calls `node->ExecProcNode(node)` which is a function pointer set during ExecInitNode()\n  - `MultiExecProcNode()` — Alternative dispatch for operations returning sets (bitmap operations)\n  - `ExecEndNode()` — Cleanup dispatch\n- **src/backend/executor/nodeXXX.c** — 50+ node executor implementations, including:\n  - Scan nodes: `nodeSeqscan.c`, `nodeIndexscan.c`, `nodeBitmapHeapscan.c`\n  - Join nodes: `nodeNestloop.c`, `nodeMergejoin.c`, `nodeHashjoin.c`\n  - Aggregate nodes: `nodeAgg.c`, `nodeGroup.c`, `nodeWindowAgg.c`\n  - Sort/Material: `nodeSort.c`, `nodeMaterial.c`\n  - Modification: `nodeModifyTable.c`\n  - Set operations: `nodeSetOp.c`, `nodeAppend.c`\n- **src/backend/executor/execExpr.c** — Expression evaluation engine; `ExecInitExpr()` compiles expressions to flat step array; `ExecExprInterp()` interprets steps\n- **src/backend/executor/execScan.c** — Common scan node infrastructure\n- **src/backend/executor/execTuples.c** — Tuple slot management\n- **src/backend/executor/execUtils.c** — General executor utilities\n\n### Node Type Definitions\n- **src/include/nodes/parsenodes.h** — Parse tree node definitions (RawStmt, Expr, etc.)\n- **src/include/nodes/plannodes.h** — Plan tree node definitions\n- **src/include/nodes/execnodes.h** — Executor state node definitions (PlanState, ScanState, JoinState, etc.)\n- **src/include/executor/execdesc.h** — QueryDesc definition\n- **src/include/executor/executor.h** — Executor API and inline functions (ExecProcNode, etc.)\n\n---\n\n## Dependency Chain\n\n### Entry: Query Reception to Execution\n\n```\nexec_simple_query() [src/backend/tcop/postgres.c:1011]\n    ↓\n1. PARSING STAGE\n    ↓\npg_parse_query() [src/backend/tcop/postgres.c:603]\n    ↓\nraw_parser() [src/backend/parser/parser.c]\n    ↓\nUses scan.l (lexer) + gram.y (grammar)\n    ↓\nReturns: List of RawStmt nodes\n\n    ↓\n2. SEMANTIC ANALYSIS STAGE\n    ↓\npg_analyze_and_rewrite_fixedparams() [src/backend/tcop/postgres.c:665]\n    ↓\nparse_analyze_fixedparams() [src/backend/parser/analyze.c:105]\n    ↓\nTransforms RawStmt → Query\nUses parse_*.c modules for detailed analysis\nReturns: Single Query node\n\n    ↓\n3. PLANNING STAGE\n    ↓\npg_plan_queries() [src/backend/tcop/postgres.c:970]\n    ↓\npg_plan_query() [src/backend/tcop/postgres.c:882]\n    ↓\nplanner() [src/backend/optimizer/plan/planner.c:287]\n    ↓\nstandard_planner() [src/backend/optimizer/plan/planner.c:303]\n    ├─ subquery_planner() [src/backend/optimizer/plan/planmain.c]\n    │   ├─ PHASE 1: Path Generation via allpaths.c\n    │   │   ├─ generate_base_rel_paths() - base relation paths\n    │   │   ├─ add_other_rel_paths() - other relation types\n    │   │   └─ add_paths_to_joinrel() - join paths\n    │   │       └─ Uses joinpath.c (nested loop, merge, hash)\n    │   │       └─ Uses costsize.c for cost estimation\n    │   ├─ Builds RelOptInfo with alternative Paths\n    │   └─ Returns Root (PlannerInfo) with final RelOptInfo\n    │\n    ├─ fetch_upper_rel() - fetches final RelOptInfo\n    ├─ get_cheapest_fractional_path() - selects best Path\n    │\n    └─ PHASE 2: Plan Creation via createplan.c\n        ├─ create_plan() [src/backend/optimizer/plan/createplan.c]\n        │   ├─ Recursively converts Path → Plan\n        │   ├─ Dispatch via switch on Path type\n        │   └─ Populates Plan node fields\n        └─ set_plan_references() - adjusts variable references\n\nReturns: PlannedStmt (contains Plan tree + metadata)\n\n    ↓\n5. EXECUTION STAGE\n    ↓\nPortalRun() [src/backend/tcop/pquery.c]\n    ↓\nProcessQuery() [src/backend/tcop/pquery.c:137]\n    ↓\nCreateQueryDesc() [src/backend/tcop/pquery.c:68]\n    Returns: QueryDesc = {plannedstmt, sourceText, snapshot, dest, params, ...}\n    ↓\nExecutorStart() [src/backend/executor/execMain.c:122]\n    ↓\nstandard_ExecutorStart() [src/backend/executor/execMain.c:141]\n    ├─ CreateExecutorState() - creates EState\n    └─ InitPlan() [src/backend/executor/execMain.c]\n        └─ ExecInitNode(planTree, estate, eflags)\n            ├─ VOLCANO DISPATCH: Switch on node tag\n            ├─ For each node type, calls ExecInitXxx()\n            │   └─ Each ExecInitXxx recursively calls ExecInitNode() on children\n            └─ Builds parallel PlanState tree\n [src/backend/executor/execMain.c]\n        └─ Loop: ExecProcNode(topNode)\n            ├─ VOLCANO PULL: Inline dispatch in executor.h:310\n            │   └─ Calls node->ExecProcNode(node)\n            ├─ Each node's ExecXxx() function\n            │   ├─ Calls ExecProcNode() on children to pull input tuples\n            │   ├─ Processes (filter, project, join, aggregate, etc.)\n            │   └─ Returns output TupleTableSlot or NULL\n            └─ Repeats until ExecProcNode returns NULL (EOF)\n    ↓\nExecutorFinish() [src/backend/executor/execMain.c]\n    └─ ExecFinishNode() - finalize aggregates, etc.\n    ↓\nExecutorEnd() [src/backend/executor/execMain.c]\n    └─ ExecEndNode() - cleanup via switch dispatch\n```\n\n---\n\n## Analysis\n\n### Design Patterns Identified\n\n#### 1. **Volcano-Style Execution Model (Iterator Model)**\nPostgreSQL implements the classic Volcano/Cascades iterator execution model:\n- Each plan node acts as an iterator with three main operations:\n  - **Init** (`ExecInitNode`, dispatches to `ExecInitXxx`): Initialize state\n  - **Next** (`ExecProcNode`, dispatches to node-specific executor function): Pull one tuple\n  - **End** (`ExecEndNode`, dispatches to `ExecEndXxx`): Clean up\n\n- **Pull-based pipeline**: Execution flows bottom-up; parent nodes pull tuples from children via `ExecProcNode()` calls\n- **Tuple-at-a-time processing**: Each `ExecProcNode()` call returns exactly one tuple (or NULL for EOF)\n- **Function pointer dispatch**: During init, each PlanState node gets a function pointer (`ExecProcNode`) pointing to its executor function\n- **Recursive composition**: Complex queries are built from simple node types; nodes at all levels follow the same iterator interface\n\nThe inline `ExecProcNode()` (executor.h:310) is the performance-critical dispatch mechanism:\n```c\nstatic inline TupleTableSlot *\nExecProcNode(PlanState *node) {\n    if (node->chgParam != NULL)\n        ExecReScan(node);\n    return node->ExecProcNode(node);  // Function pointer dispatch\n}\n```\n\nThis design enables:\n- **Modularity**: New node types added by implementing Init/Next/End functions\n- **Composability**: Complex execution plans from simple, reusable components\n- **Memory efficiency**: Streaming tuple processing (no materializing entire result sets)\n\n#### 2. **Two-Phase Optimization**\nThe planner decomposes optimization into distinct phases:\n\n**Phase 1 – Path Generation (allpaths.c)**\n- Generates candidate execution paths for each relation and join combination\n- Each Path represents one possible way to access/process data\n- Paths include cost information (startup + total cost estimates)\n- Examples: SeqScan path, IndexScan path, BitmapIndexScan path\n- Joins generate: NestLoopPath, MergeJoinPath, HashJoinPath\n- Products: RelOptInfo with list of Paths; winner selected by cost\n\n**Phase 2 – Plan Creation (createplan.c)**\n- Converts optimal Path to executable Plan tree\n- `create_plan()` recursively traverses Path tree\n- Populates Plan nodes with node-specific initialization data\n- Example: HashJoinPath → HashJoin plan with hash table building strategy\n- Result: Plan tree ready for execution (schema-aware, all properties resolved)\n\nThis two-phase separation provides:\n- **Search space exploration** without committing to execution representation\n- **Cost-based decisions** with flexible path representations\n- **Clean interface** between optimization and execution (Path vs Plan)\n\n#### 3. **Read-Only Plan Trees**\n- Plan tree (src/include/nodes/plannodes.h) is completely immutable during execution\n- All mutable state is in the parallel PlanState tree (execnodes.h)\n- Enables safe plan caching and reuse across multiple executions\n- Separation of concerns: Planner produces schema; Executor manages state\n\n#### 4. **Expression Compilation to Flat Form**\n- Expr trees (parse tree representation) are compiled to flat ExprEvalStep arrays during ExecutorStart\n- `ExecInitExpr()` builds ExprState with steps[] array\n- Benefits:\n  - Reduces tree-walk overhead during evaluation\n  - Single-function interpretation of expressions\n  - Enables JIT compilation without interpreter overhead\n  - Precomputes invariant information\n\n#### 5. **State Tree Mirrors Plan Tree Structure**\n- During ExecutorStart, a PlanState tree is built with identical structure to Plan tree\n- Each Plan node → corresponding PlanState node type\n- Example: `Plan::Append` → `PlanState::AppendState`\n- PlanState holds all mutable data needed during execution\n- Allows plan reuse across multiple executions\n\n### Component Responsibilities\n\n**Traffic Cop (postgres.c:1011)**\n- Receives raw SQL string\n- Coordinates entire pipeline\n- Manages transaction context\n- Handles command completion and result delivery\n\n**Parser (parser.c + scan.l + gram.y)**\n- **Responsibilities**: Lexical + syntactic analysis\n- **Input**: SQL text string\n- **Output**: Parse tree (RawStmt with generic structure)\n- **Mechanism**: Flex lexer (scan.l) tokenizes; Bison parser (gram.y) builds tree\n- **Key Property**: No semantic validation; purely structural\n\n**Semantic Analyzer (analyze.c + parse_*.c)**\n- **Responsibilities**: Semantic validation, type checking, name resolution\n- **Input**: RawStmt (untyped parse tree)\n- **Output**: Query (semantically valid, type-checked)\n- **Process**:\n  - Validates table/column names against schema\n  - Type-checks expressions and coerces as needed\n  - Resolves ambiguous names\n  - Processes special clauses (aggregates, window functions, CTEs)\n- **Key Property**: Single Query per input RawStmt (usually)\n\n**Query Rewriter (rewriteHandler.c)**\n- **Responsibilities**: Rule application, view expansion, security policies\n- **Input**: Query (semantic tree)\n- **Output**: List of Queries (0..n due to expansion)\n- **Examples**:\n  - View → subquery in FROM\n  - Rule → additional auxiliary queries\n  - RLS policies → WHERE clause additions\n- **Key Property**: May expand 1 Query into many (SELECT + INSERT rule → 2 queries)\n\n**Planner - Phase 1 (allpaths.c)**\n- **Responsibilities**: Generate candidate execution paths\n- **Input**: Query (semantic tree)\n- **Scope**: Base relations, joins, aggregations, etc.\n- **Process**:\n  - `generate_base_rel_paths()`: Paths for single tables\n  - `add_paths_to_joinrel()`: Join paths via nested loop, merge, hash\n  - Cost estimation via `cost_*()` functions\n- **Output**: RelOptInfo with alternative Paths (no execution specifics yet)\n\n**Planner - Phase 2 (createplan.c)**\n- **Responsibilities**: Convert optimal Path to Plan\n- **Input**: Best Path from Phase 1\n- **Process**: Recursive `create_plan()` dispatch\n  - Path type → Plan type\n  - Populates Plan node with execution parameters\n  - Example: HashPath → HashJoin with hash function, key columns\n- **Output**: Plan tree (execution-ready, immutable)\n\n**Executor - Init (execMain.c + execProcnode.c)**\n- **Responsibilities**: Build execution state tree\n- **Input**: Plan tree\n- **Process**: ExecInitNode recursive dispatch\n  - Each Plan node → PlanState node\n  - Compile expressions to ExprState\n  - Allocate runtime data structures\n  - Set up function pointers (ExecProcNode)\n- **Output**: PlanState tree with initialized state\n\n**Executor - Run (execMain.c + execProcnode.c + nodeXXX.c)**\n- **Responsibilities**: Pull tuples through pipeline\n- **Mechanism**: ExecProcNode inline dispatch\n  - Calls node function pointers\n  - Each node pulls from children\n  - Processes (filter, project, join, aggregate)\n  - Returns tuples or NULL (EOF)\n- **Key Property**: Tuple-at-a-time; streaming; no intermediate materialization (unless Sort, Agg, etc.)\n\n**Executor - End (execProcnode.c)**\n- **Responsibilities**: Clean up resources\n- **Process**: ExecEndNode recursive dispatch\n- **Handles**: Closing scans, freeing buffers, finalizing aggregates\n\n### Data Flow: Type Transformations\n\n```\nSQL String\n    ↓\n    └→ raw_parser() [scan.l + gram.y]\n        ↓\n        └→ RawStmt (untyped generic structure)\n            - Minimal semantic info\n            - No type checking\n            - No name resolution\n            ↓\n            └→ parse_analyze() [analyze.c + parse_*.c]\n                ↓\n                └→ Query (type-checked, name-resolved)\n                    - Full semantic information\n                    - Expression types resolved\n                    - Table/column references validated\n                    ↓\n                    └→ QueryRewrite() [rewriteHandler.c]\n                        ↓\n                        └→ Query (possibly expanded)\n                            - Rules applied\n                            - Views expanded\n                            - Security policies injected\n                            ↓\n                            └→ standard_planner() [planner.c]\n                                ├─ Phase 1: allpaths.c\n                                │   └→ RelOptInfo (Paths with cost)\n                                └─ Phase 2: createplan.c\n                                    ↓\n                                    └→ PlannedStmt (Plan tree + metadata)\n                                        - Executable plan\n                                        - All joins, aggregates planned\n                                        - Immutable during execution\n                                        ↓\n                                        └→ ExecutorStart() [execMain.c]\n                                            ↓\n                                            └→ ExecInitNode() [execProcnode.c]\n                                                ↓\n                                                └→ PlanState tree\n                                                    - Runtime state\n                                                    - ExprState compiled\n                                                    - Function pointers set\n                                                    ↓\n                                                    └→ ExecutorRun()\n                                                        └→ ExecProcNode() loop\n                                                            ↓\n                                                            └→ Tuples (result set)\n```\n\n### Interface Contracts Between Components\n\n**Parser → Semantic Analyzer**\n- **Contract**: RawStmt with untyped expressions\n- **Guarantees**: Syntactically valid; may contain name/type errors\n- **Properties**: Generic structure (no knowledge of command type)\n\n**Semantic Analyzer → Rewriter**\n- **Contract**: Query with resolved types and names\n- **Guarantees**: Semantically valid within current schema; expressions typed\n- **Properties**: One-to-one mapping (usually) with input\n\n**Rewriter → Planner**\n- **Contract**: Query (may be from rewriter expansion)\n- **Guarantees**: Fully analyzed; ready for optimization\n- **Properties**: Multiple queries possible (parallel independent optimization)\n\n**Planner → Executor**\n- **Contract**: PlannedStmt with Plan tree\n- **Guarantees**: Optimal execution path selected; all joins/aggregates planned\n- **Properties**: Immutable; can be cached and reused\n\n**Executor Init → Executor Run**\n- **Contract**: PlanState tree with initialized state\n- **Guarantees**: All runtime structures allocated; expressions compiled\n- **Properties**: State tree mirrors plan structure; function pointers active\n\n### Volcano-Style Executor Dispatch (execProcnode.c)\n\nThe core dispatch mechanism at execution time is the **pull model**:\n\n**ExecProcNode inline dispatch (executor.h:310)**:\n```c\nstatic inline TupleTableSlot *\nExecProcNode(PlanState *node) {\n    if (node->chgParam != NULL)\n        ExecReScan(node);\n    return node->ExecProcNode(node);  // Function pointer\n}\n```\n\n**Dispatch during init** (`ExecInitNode`, execProcnode.c:142):\n```\nswitch (nodeTag(plan)) {\n    case T_SeqScan:\n        result = (PlanState *)ExecInitSeqScan((SeqScan *)node, ...);\n        // This sets: result->ExecProcNode = ExecSeqScan\n        break;\n    case T_NestLoop:\n        result = (PlanState *)ExecInitNestLoop((NestLoop *)node, ...);\n        // This sets: result->ExecProcNode = ExecNestLoop\n        break;\n    ...\n}\n```\n\n**Execution via function pointers** (nodeXXX.c):\n- `ExecSeqScan()` [nodeSeqscan.c]: Fetches tuples from heap sequentially\n- `ExecNestLoop()` [nodeNestloop.c]: Pulls from outer, for each outer pulls from inner, returns joined tuples\n- `ExecAgg()` [nodeAgg.c]: Accumulates tuples, returns aggregated results\n- `ExecSort()` [nodeSort.c]: Collects all input, sorts, returns in order\n- Each function:\n  1. Calls `ExecProcNode()` on children to get input tuples\n  2. Processes the tuple (filtering, projection, joining, aggregating)\n  3. Returns result tuple or NULL (EOF)\n\n**Pipeline execution in ExecutePlan()** (execMain.c:~350):\n```\nwhile (true) {\n    slot = ExecProcNode(topNode);  // Pull from root\n    if (TupIsNull(slot)) break;     // EOF\n    dest->receiveSlot(slot);         // Send to client\n}\n```\n\nThis creates a **demand-driven pipeline**:\n- Tuples flow bottom-up (pulled by parents)\n- No global queue/buffer (except for Sort, Agg, etc.)\n- Natural backpressure (if parent slow, child waits)\n- Scales to large result sets (streaming)\n\n---\n\n## Summary\n\nPostgreSQL implements a **classic multi-stage query execution pipeline** with clear separation of concerns. The **parser** (lexer + grammar) produces untyped parse trees; the **semantic analyzer** validates and types them; the **rewriter** applies rules and view expansion; the **planner** executes two-phase optimization (path generation then plan creation) to find the optimal execution strategy; and the **Volcano-style executor** pulls tuples through a tree of iterator nodes, with each node dispatched via function pointers to its type-specific implementation. This architecture achieves modularity, composability, and efficiency through clean interfaces between pipeline stages and a demand-driven execution model that streams results without materializing intermediate datasets.\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":7,"cache_creation_input_tokens":3091,"cache_read_input_tokens":98180,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":3091},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"545eac15-e645-4e2d-a57d-4e018a47a4e9","uuid":"fd029a89-c677-43bf-ad66-6170fcaed531"}

= {plannedstmt, sourceText, snapshot, dest, params, ...}\n    ↓\nExecutorStart() [src/backend/executor/execMain.c:122]\n    ↓\nstandard_ExecutorStart() [src/backend/executor/execMain.c:141]\n    ├─ aggregates, etc.\n    ↓\nExecutorEnd() [src/backend/executor/execMain.c]\n    └─ ExecEndNode() - cleanup via switch dispatch\n```\n\n---\n\n## Analysis\n\n### Design Patterns Identified\n\n#### 1. **Volcano-Style Execution Model (Iterator Model)**\nPostgreSQL implements the classic Volcano/Cascades iterator execution model:\n- Each plan node acts as an iterator with three main operations:\n  - **Init** (`ExecInitNode`, dispatches to `ExecInitXxx`): Initialize state\n  - **Next** (`ExecProcNode`, dispatches to node-specific executor function): Pull one tuple\n  - **End** (`ExecEndNode`, dispatches to `ExecEndXxx`): Clean up\n\n- **Pull-based pipeline**: Execution flows bottom-up; parent nodes pull tuples from children via `ExecProcNode()` calls\n- **Tuple-at-a-time processing**: Each `ExecProcNode()` call returns exactly one tuple (or NULL for EOF)\n- **Function pointer dispatch**: During init, each PlanState node gets a function pointer (`ExecProcNode`) pointing to its executor function\n- **Recursive composition**: Complex queries are built from simple node types; nodes at all levels follow the same iterator interface\n\nThe inline `ExecProcNode()` (executor.h:310) is the performance-critical dispatch mechanism:\n```c\nstatic inline TupleTableSlot *\nExecProcNode(PlanState *node) {\n    if (node->chgParam != NULL)\n        ExecReScan(node);\n    return node->ExecProcNode(node);  // Function pointer dispatch\n}\n```\n\nThis design enables:\n- **Modularity**: New node types added by implementing Init/Next/End functions\n- **Composability**: Complex execution plans from simple, reusable components\n- **Memory efficiency**: Streaming tuple processing (no materializing entire result sets)\n\n#### 2. **Two-Phase Optimization**\nThe planner decomposes optimization into distinct phases:\n\n**Phase 1 – Path Generation (allpaths.c)**\n- Generates candidate execution paths for each relation and join combination\n- Each Path represents one possible way to access/process data\n- Paths include cost information (startup + total cost estimates)\n- Examples: SeqScan path, IndexScan path, BitmapIndexScan path\n- Joins generate: NestLoopPath, MergeJoinPath, HashJoinPath\n- Products: RelOptInfo with list of Paths; winner selected by cost\n\n**Phase 2 – Plan Creation (createplan.c)**\n- Converts optimal Path to executable Plan tree\n- `create_plan()` recursively traverses Path tree\n- Populates Plan nodes with node-specific initialization data\n- Example: HashJoinPath → HashJoin plan with hash table building strategy\n- Result: Plan tree ready for execution (schema-aware, all properties resolved)\n\nThis two-phase separation provides:\n- **Search space exploration** without committing to execution representation\n- **Cost-based decisions** with flexible path representations\n- **Clean interface** between optimization and execution (Path vs Plan)\n\n#### 3. **Read-Only Plan Trees**\n- Plan tree (src/include/nodes/plannodes.h) is completely immutable during execution\n- All mutable state is in the parallel PlanState tree (execnodes.h)\n- Enables safe plan caching and reuse across multiple executions\n- Separation of concerns: Planner produces schema; Executor manages state\n\n#### 4. **Expression Compilation to Flat Form**\n- Expr trees (parse tree representation) are compiled to flat ExprEvalStep arrays during ExecutorStart\n- `ExecInitExpr()` builds ExprState with steps[] array\n- Benefits:\n  - Reduces tree-walk overhead during evaluation\n  - Single-function interpretation of expressions\n  - Enables JIT compilation without interpreter overhead\n  - Precomputes invariant information\n\n#### 5. **State Tree Mirrors Plan Tree Structure**\n- During ExecutorStart, a PlanState tree is built with identical structure to Plan tree\n- Each Plan node → corresponding PlanState node type\n- Example: `Plan::Append` → `PlanState::AppendState`\n- PlanState holds all mutable data needed during execution\n- Allows plan reuse across multiple executions\n\n### Component Responsibilities\n\n**Traffic Cop (postgres.c:1011)**\n- Receives raw SQL string\n- Coordinates entire pipeline\n- Manages transaction context\n- Handles command completion and result delivery\n\n**Parser (parser.c + scan.l + gram.y)**\n- **Responsibilities**: Lexical + syntactic analysis\n- **Input**: SQL text string\n- **Output**: Parse tree (RawStmt with generic structure)\n- **Mechanism**: Flex lexer (scan.l) tokenizes; Bison parser (gram.y) builds tree\n- **Key Property**: No semantic validation; purely structural\n\n**Semantic Analyzer (analyze.c + parse_*.c)**\n- **Responsibilities**: Semantic validation, type checking, name resolution\n- **Input**: RawStmt (untyped parse tree)\n- **Output**: Query (semantically valid, type-checked)\n- **Process**:\n  - Validates table/column names against schema\n  - Type-checks expressions and coerces as needed\n  - Resolves ambiguous names\n  - Processes special clauses (aggregates, window functions, CTEs)\n- **Key Property**: Single Query per input RawStmt (usually)\n\n**Query Rewriter (rewriteHandler.c)**\n- **Responsibilities**: Rule application, view expansion, security policies\n- **Input**: Query (semantic tree)\n- **Output**: List of Queries (0..n due to expansion)\n- **Examples**:\n  - View → subquery in FROM\n  - Rule → additional auxiliary queries\n  - RLS policies → WHERE clause additions\n- **Key Property**: May expand 1 Query into many (SELECT + INSERT rule → 2 queries)\n\n**Planner - Phase 1 (allpaths.c)**\n- **Responsibilities**: Generate candidate execution paths\n- **Input**: Query (semantic tree)\n- **Scope**: Base relations, joins, aggregations, etc.\n- **Process**:\n  - `generate_base_rel_paths()`: Paths for single tables\n  - `add_paths_to_joinrel()`: Join paths via nested loop, merge, hash\n  - Cost estimation via `cost_*()` functions\n- **Output**: RelOptInfo with alternative Paths (no execution specifics yet)\n\n**Planner - Phase 2 (createplan.c)**\n- **Responsibilities**: Convert optimal Path to Plan\n- **Input**: Best Path from Phase 1\n- **Process**: Recursive `create_plan()` dispatch\n  - Path type → Plan type\n  - Populates Plan node with execution parameters\n  - Example: HashPath → HashJoin with hash function, key columns\n- **Output**: Plan tree (execution-ready, immutable)\n\n**Executor - Init (execMain.c + execProcnode.c)**\n- **Responsibilities**: Build execution state tree\n- **Input**: Plan tree\n- **Process**: ExecInitNode recursive dispatch\n  - Each Plan node → PlanState node\n  - Compile expressions to ExprState\n  - Allocate runtime data structures\n  - Set up function pointers (ExecProcNode)\n- **Output**: PlanState tree with initialized state\n\n**Executor - Run (execMain.c + execProcnode.c + nodeXXX.c)**\n- **Responsibilities**: Pull tuples through pipeline\n- **Mechanism**: ExecProcNode inline dispatch\n  - Calls node function pointers\n  - Each node pulls from children\n  - Processes (filter, project, join, aggregate)\n  - Returns tuples or NULL (EOF)\n- **Key Property**: Tuple-at-a-time; streaming; no intermediate materialization (unless Sort, Agg, etc.)\n\n**Executor - End (execProcnode.c)**\n- **Responsibilities**: Clean up resources\n- **Process**: ExecEndNode recursive dispatch\n- **Handles**: Closing scans, freeing buffers, finalizing aggregates\n\n### Data Flow: Type Transformations\n\n```\nSQL String\n    ↓\n    └→ raw_parser() [scan.l + gram.y]\n        ↓\n        └→ RawStmt (untyped generic structure)\n            - Minimal semantic info\n            - No type checking\n            - No name resolution\n            ↓\n            └→ parse_analyze() [analyze.c + parse_*.c]\n                ↓\n                └→ Query (type-checked, name-resolved)\n                    - Full semantic information\n                    - Expression types resolved\n                    - Table/column references validated\n                    ↓\n                    └→ QueryRewrite() [rewriteHandler.c]\n                        ↓\n                        └→ Query (possibly expanded)\n                            - Rules applied\n                            - Views expanded\n                            - Security policies injected\n                            ↓\n                            └→ standard_planner() [planner.c]\n                                ├─ Phase 1: allpaths.c\n                                │   └→ RelOptInfo (Paths with cost)\n                                └─ Phase 2: createplan.c\n                                    ↓\n                                    └→ PlannedStmt (Plan tree + metadata)\n                                        - Executable plan\n                                        - All joins, aggregates planned\n                                        - Immutable during execution\n                                        ↓\n                                        └→ ExecutorStart() [execMain.c]\n                                            ↓\n                                            └→ ExecInitNode() [execProcnode.c]\n                                                ↓\n                                                └→ PlanState tree\n                                                    - Runtime state\n                                                    - ExprState compiled\n                                                    - Function pointers set\n                                                    ↓\n                                                    └→ ExecutorRun()\n                                                        └→ ExecProcNode() loop\n                                                            ↓\n                                                            └→ Tuples (result set)\n```\n\n### Interface Contracts Between Components\n\n**Parser → Semantic Analyzer**\n- **Contract**: RawStmt with untyped expressions\n- **Guarantees**: Syntactically valid; may contain name/type errors\n- **Properties**: Generic structure (no knowledge of command type)\n\n**Semantic Analyzer → Rewriter**\n- **Contract**: Query with resolved types and names\n- **Guarantees**: Semantically valid within current schema; expressions typed\n- **Properties**: One-to-one mapping (usually) with input\n\n**Rewriter → Planner**\n- **Contract**: Query (may be from rewriter expansion)\n- **Guarantees**: Fully analyzed; ready for optimization\n- **Properties**: Multiple queries possible (parallel independent optimization)\n\n**Planner → Executor**\n- **Contract**: PlannedStmt with Plan tree\n- **Guarantees**: Optimal execution path selected; all joins/aggregates planned\n- **Properties**: Immutable; can be cached and reused\n\n**Executor Init → Executor Run**\n- **Contract**: PlanState tree with initialized state\n- **Guarantees**: All runtime structures allocated; expressions compiled\n- **Properties**: State tree mirrors plan structure; function pointers active\n\n### Volcano-Style Executor Dispatch (execProcnode.c)\n\nThe core dispatch mechanism at execution time is the **pull model**:\n\n**ExecProcNode inline dispatch (executor.h:310)**:\n```c\nstatic inline TupleTableSlot *\nExecProcNode(PlanState *node) {\n    if (node->chgParam != NULL)\n        ExecReScan(node);\n    return node->ExecProcNode(node);  // Function pointer\n}\n```\n\n**Dispatch during init** (`ExecInitNode`, execProcnode.c:142):\n```\nswitch (nodeTag(plan)) {\n    case T_SeqScan:\n        result = (PlanState *)ExecInitSeqScan((SeqScan *)node, ...);\n        // This sets: result->ExecProcNode = ExecSeqScan\n        break;\n    case T_NestLoop:\n        result = (PlanState *)ExecInitNestLoop((NestLoop *)node, ...);\n        // This sets: result->ExecProcNode = ExecNestLoop\n        break;\n    ...\n}\n```\n\n**Execution via function pointers** (nodeXXX.c):\n- `ExecSeqScan()` [nodeSeqscan.c]: Fetches tuples from heap sequentially\n- `ExecNestLoop()` [nodeNestloop.c]: Pulls from outer, for each outer pulls from inner, returns joined tuples\n- `ExecAgg()` [nodeAgg.c]: Accumulates tuples, returns aggregated results\n- `ExecSort()` [nodeSort.c]: Collects all input, sorts, returns in order\n- Each function:\n  1. Calls `ExecProcNode()` on children to get input tuples\n  2. Processes the tuple (filtering, projection, joining, aggregating)\n  3. Returns result tuple or NULL (EOF)\n\n**Pipeline execution in ExecutePlan()** (execMain.c:~350):\n```\nwhile (true) {\n    slot = ExecProcNode(topNode);  // Pull from root\n    if (TupIsNull(slot)) break;     // EOF\n    dest->receiveSlot(slot);         // Send to client\n}\n```\n\nThis creates a **demand-driven pipeline**:\n- Tuples flow bottom-up (pulled by parents)\n- No global queue/buffer (except for Sort, Agg, etc.)\n- Natural backpressure (if parent slow, child waits)\n- Scales to large result sets (streaming)\n\n---\n\n## Summary\n\nPostgreSQL implements a **classic multi-stage query execution pipeline** with clear separation of concerns. The **parser** (lexer + grammar) produces untyped parse trees; the **semantic analyzer** validates and types them; the **rewriter** applies rules and view expansion; the **planner** executes two-phase optimization (path generation then plan creation) to find the optimal execution strategy; and the **Volcano-style executor** pulls tuples through a tree of iterator nodes, with each node dispatched via function pointers to its type-specific implementation. This architecture achieves modularity, composability, and efficiency through clean interfaces between pipeline stages and a demand-driven execution model that streams results without materializing intermediate datasets.\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
